This movement has been particularly evident in logistics, where the provision of transport, storage, and inventory control is increasingly subcontracted to specialists or logistics partners. Also, managing and controlling this network of partners and suppliers requires a blend of central and local involvement: strategic decisions are taken centrally, while the monitoring and control of supplier performance and day-to-day liaison with logistics partners are best managed locally.</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Performance_measurement" title="Performance measurement">Performance measurement</a></dt>
<dd>Experts found a strong relationship from the largest arcs of supplier and customer integration to market share and profitability. Taking advantage of supplier capabilities and emphasizing a long-term supply chain perspective in customer relationships can both be correlated with a firm's performance. As logistics competency becomes a critical factor in creating and maintaining competitive advantage, measuring logistics performance becomes increasingly important, because the difference between profitable and unprofitable operations becomes narrower. <a href="/wiki/Kearney_(consulting_firm)" title="Kearney (consulting firm)">A.T. Kearney Consultants</a> (1985) noted that firms engaging in comprehensive performance measurement realized improvements in overall productivity. According to experts,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (August 2023)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> internal measures are generally collected and analyzed by the firm, including cost, customer service, productivity, asset measurement, and quality. External performance is measured through customer perception measures and "<a href="/wiki/Best_practice" title="Best practice">best practice</a>" benchmarking.</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Warehouse_management_system" title="Warehouse management system">Warehousing management</a></dt>
<dd>To reduce a company's cost and expenses, warehousing management is concerned with storage, reducing manpower cost, dispatching authority with on time delivery, loading and unloading facilities with proper area, inventory management system etc.</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Workflow_management_system" title="Workflow management system">Workflow management</a></dt>
<dd>Integrating suppliers and customers tightly into a <a href="/wiki/Workflow" title="Workflow">workflow</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Business_process" title="Business process">business process</a>) and thereby achieving an efficient and effective supply chain is a key goal of <a href="/wiki/Workflow" title="Workflow">workflow</a> management.</dd></dl>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Theories">Theories</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Theories"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There are gaps in the literature on supply chain management studies at present.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A few authors, such as Halldorsson et al.,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ketchen and Hult (2006),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Lavassani et al. (2009), have tried to provide theoretical foundations for different areas related to supply chain by employing organizational theories, which may include the following:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Resource-based_view" title="Resource-based view">Resource-based view</a> (RBV)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Transaction cost analysis (TCA)</li>
<li>Knowledge-based view (KBV)</li>
<li>Strategic choice theory (SCT)</li>
<li>Agency theory (AT)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Channel_coordination" title="Channel coordination">Channel coordination</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Institutional_theory" title="Institutional theory">Institutional theory</a> (InT)</li>
<li>Systems theory (ST)</li>
<li>Network perspective (NP)</li>
<li>Materials logistics management (MLM)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_(business)" class="mw-redirect" title="Just-in-time (business)">Just-in-time</a> (JIT)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Material_requirements_planning" title="Material requirements planning">Material requirements planning</a> (MRP)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Theory_of_constraints" title="Theory of constraints">Theory of constraints</a> (TOC)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Total_quality_management" title="Total quality management">Total quality management</a> (TQM)</li>
<li>Agile manufacturing</li>
<li>Time-based competition (TBC)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quick_response_manufacturing" title="Quick response manufacturing">Quick response manufacturing</a> (QRM)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">Customer relationship management</a> (CRM)</li>
<li>Requirements chain management  (RCM)</li>
<li>Dynamic Capabilities Theory</li>
<li>Dynamic Management Theory</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Available-to-promise" title="Available-to-promise">Available-to-promise</a>  (ATP)</li>
<li>Supply Chain Roadmap<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Optimal Positioning of the Delivery Window (OPDW)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>However, the <a href="/wiki/Unit_of_analysis" title="Unit of analysis">unit of analysis</a> of most of these theories is not the supply chain but rather another system, such as the firm or the supplier-buyer relationship. Among the few exceptions is the <a href="/wiki/Relational_view" title="Relational view">relational view</a>, which outlines a theory for considering dyads and networks of firms as a key unit of analysis for explaining superior individual firm performance (Dyer and Singh, 1998).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Organization_and_governance">Organization and governance</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Organization and governance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The management of supply chains involve a number of specific challenges regarding the organization of relationships among the different partners along the value chain. Formal and informal governance mechanisms are central elements in the management of supply chain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Particular combinations of governance mechanisms may impact the relational dynamics within the supply chain. The need for <a href="/wiki/Interdisciplinarity" title="Interdisciplinarity">interdisciplinarity</a> in SCM research has been pointed out by academics in the field.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Supply_chain_centroids">Supply chain centroids</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Supply chain centroids"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the study of supply chain management, the concept of <a href="/wiki/Centroid" title="Centroid">centroids</a> has become a useful economic consideration. In <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, a centroid is the <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_mean" title="Arithmetic mean">arithmetic mean</a> position of all the points in a <a href="/wiki/Plane_figure" class="mw-redirect" title="Plane figure">plane figure</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For supply chain management, a centroid is a location with a high proportion of a country's population and a high proportion of its manufacturing, generally within 500&#160;mi (805&#160;km). In the US, two major supply chain centroids have been defined, one near <a href="/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio" title="Dayton, Ohio">Dayton, Ohio</a>, and a second near <a href="/wiki/Riverside,_California" title="Riverside, California">Riverside, California</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The centroid near Dayton is particularly important because it is closest to the population center of the US and Canada. Dayton is within 500&#160;miles of 60% of the US population and manufacturing capacity, as well as 60% of Canada's population.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-daytondailynews.com&#95;113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daytondailynews.com-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The region includes the interchange between <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70" title="Interstate 70">I-70</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75" title="Interstate 75">I-75</a>, one of the busiest in the nation, with 154,000 vehicles passing through per day, of which 30–35% are trucks hauling goods. In addition, the I-75 corridor is home to the busiest north–south rail route east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-daytondailynews.com&#95;113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daytondailynews.com-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A supply chain is the network of all the individuals, organizations, resources, activities and technology involved in the creation and sale of a product. A supply chain encompasses everything from the delivery of source materials from the supplier to the manufacturer through to its eventual delivery to the end user. The supply chain segment involved with getting the finished product from the manufacturer to the consumer is known as the distribution channel.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Wal-Mart_strategic_sourcing_approaches">Wal-Mart strategic sourcing approaches</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Wal-Mart strategic sourcing approaches"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<table class="box-Off&#95;topic plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/120px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40"></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>may contain material <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Guide_to_writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Guide to writing better articles">unrelated to the topic of the article</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> or discuss this issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Supply_chain_management" title="Talk:Supply chain management">talk page</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Wal-Mart</a> announced a big change in its sourcing strategy. Initially, Wal-Mart relied on intermediaries in the sourcing process. It bought only 20% of its stock directly, but the rest were bought through the intermediaries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceB&#95;115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Therefore, the company came to realize that the presence of many intermediaries in the product sourcing was actually increasing the costs in the supply chain. To cut these costs, Wal-Mart decided to do away with intermediaries in the supply chain and started direct sourcing of its goods from the suppliers. Eduardo Castro-Wright, the then Vice President of Wal-Mart, set an ambitious goal of buying 80% of all Wal-Mart goods directly from the suppliers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceC&#95;116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Walmart started purchasing fruits and vegetables on a global scale, where it interacted directly with the suppliers of these goods. The company later engaged the suppliers of other goods, such as cloth and home electronics appliances, directly and eliminated the importing agents. The purchaser, in this case Wal-Mart, can easily direct the suppliers on how to manufacture certain products so that they can be acceptable to the consumers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceD&#95;117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceD-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Thus, Wal-Mart, through direct sourcing, manages to get the exact product quality as it expects, since it engages the suppliers in the producing of these products, hence quality consistency.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceC&#95;116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Using agents in the sourcing process in most cases lead to inconsistency in the quality of the products, since the agent's source the products from different manufacturers that have varying qualities.
</p><p>Wal-Mart managed to source directly 80% profit its stock; this has greatly eliminated the intermediaries and cut down the costs between 5-15%, as markups that are introduced by these middlemen in the supply chain are cut. This saves approximately $4–15 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceB&#95;115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This strategy of direct sourcing not only helped Wal-Mart in reducing the costs in the supply chain but also helped in the improvement of supply chain activities through boosting efficiency throughout the entire process. In other words, direct sourcing reduced the time that takes the company to source and stocks the products in its stock.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceC&#95;116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The presence of the intermediaries elongated the time in the process of procurement, which sometimes led to delays in the supply of the commodities in the stores, thus, customers finding empty shelves. Wal-Mart adopted this strategy of sourcing through centralizing the entire process of procurement and sourcing by setting up four global merchandising points for general goods and clothing. The company instructed all the suppliers to bring their products to these central points that are located in different markets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceD&#95;117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceD-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The procurement team assesses the quality brought by the suppliers, buys the goods, and distributes them to various regional markets. The procurement and sourcing at centralized places helped the company to consolidate the suppliers.
</p><p>The company has established four centralized points, including an office in Mexico City and Canada. Just a mere piloting test on combining the purchase of fresh apples across the United States, Mexico, and Canada led to the savings of about 10%. As a result, the company intended to increase centralization of its procurement in North America for all its fresh fruits and vegetables.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceB&#95;115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Thus, centralization of the procurement process to various points where the suppliers would be meeting with the procurement team is the latest strategy which the company is implementing, and signs show that this strategy is going to cut costs and also improve the efficiency of the procurement process.
</p><p>Strategic vendor partnerships is another strategy the company is using in the sourcing process. Wal-Mart realized that in order for it to ensure consistency in the quality of the products it offers to the consumers and also maintain a steady supply of goods in its stores at a lower cost, it had to create strategic vendor partnerships with the suppliers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceB&#95;115-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Wal-Mart identified and selected the suppliers who met its demand and at the same time offered it the best prices for the goods. It then made a strategic relationship with these vendors by offering and assuring the long-term and high volume of purchases in exchange for the lowest possible prices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceC&#95;116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Thus, the company has managed to source its products from same suppliers as bulks, but at lower prices. This enables the company to offer competitive prices for its products in its stores, hence, maintaining a competitive advantage over its competitors whose goods are a more expensive in comparison.
</p><p>Another sourcing strategy Wal-Mart uses is implementing efficient communication relationships with the vendor networks; this is necessary to improve the material flow. The company has all the contacts with the suppliers whom they communicate regularly and make dates on when the goods would be needed, so that the suppliers get ready to deliver the goods in time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The efficient communication between the company's procurement team and the inventory management team enables the company to source goods and fill its shelves on time, without causing delays and empty shelves.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In other words, the company realized that in ensuring a steady flow of the goods into the store, the suppliers have to be informed early enough, so that they can act accordingly to avoid delays in the delivery of goods.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceC&#95;116-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Thus, efficient communication is another tool which Wal-Mart is using to make the supply chain be more efficient and to cut costs.
</p><p>Cross-docking is another strategy that Wal-Mart is using to cut costs in its supply chain. Cross-docking is the process of transferring goods directly from inbound trucks to outbound trucks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReferenceB&#95;115-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When the trucks from the suppliers arrive at the distribution centers, most of the trucks are not offloaded to keep the goods in the distribution centers or warehouses; they are transferred directly to another truck designated to deliver goods to specific retail stores for sale. Cross-docking helps in saving the storage costs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Initially, the company was incurring considerable costs of storing the goods from the suppliers in its warehouses and the distributions centers to await the distribution trucks to the retail stores in various regions.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tax-efficient_supply_chain_management">Tax-efficient supply chain management</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tax-efficient supply chain management"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Tax-efficient supply chain management is a business model that considers the effect of tax in the design and implementation of supply chain management. As the consequence of globalization, cross-national businesses pay different tax rates in different countries. Due to these differences, they may legally optimize their supply chain and increase profits based on <a href="/wiki/Tax_efficiency" title="Tax efficiency">tax efficiency</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2019)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Sustainability_and_social_responsibility_in_supply_chains">Sustainability and social responsibility in supply chains</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sustainability and social responsibility in supply chains"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Supply chain networks are integral to an economy, but their health is dependent on the well-being of the environment and society.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_sustainability" title="Supply chain sustainability">Supply chain sustainability</a> is a business issue affecting an organization's supply chain or logistics network, and is frequently quantified by comparison with SECH ratings, which address social, ethical, cultural, and health footprints. These build on the triple bottom line incorporating economic, social, and environmental aspects.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The more commonly used ESG terminology represents Environment, Social and Governance. Consumers have become more aware of the environmental impact of their purchases and companies' ratings and, along with <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organizations</a> (NGOs), are setting the agenda, and beginning to push for transitions to more sustainable approaches such as <a href="/wiki/Organic_farming" title="Organic farming">organically grown</a> foods, <a href="/wiki/Anti-sweatshop" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-sweatshop">anti-sweatshop</a> labor codes, and locally produced goods that support independent and small businesses. Because supply chains may account for over 75% of a company's <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a>, many organizations are exploring ways to reduce this and thus improve their profile.
</p><p>For example, in July 2009, <a href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" class="mw-redirect" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a> announced its intentions to create a global sustainability index that would rate products according to the environmental and social impacts of their manufacturing and distribution. The index is intended to create environmental accountability in Wal-Mart's supply chain and to provide motivation and <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> for other retail companies to do the same.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>It has been reported that companies are increasingly taking environmental performance into account when selecting suppliers.  A 2011 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_Trust" title="Carbon Trust">Carbon Trust</a> found that 50% of multinationals expect to select their suppliers based upon carbon performance in the future and 29% of suppliers could lose their places on 'green supply chains' if they do not have adequate performance records on carbon.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to environmental concerns, increased globalization within global supply chains challenges human rights and worker exploitation risks within multinational corporations including forced labor and modern slavery. Textiles, agriculture, and manufacturing are some of the industries with significant labor exploitation risks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are many different methods governments, corporations, and NGOs use to prevent labor exploitation, including corporate social responsibility,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> export controls,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> import bans,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and monitoring labor standards.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The US <a href="/wiki/Dodd%E2%80%93Frank_Wall_Street_Reform_and_Consumer_Protection_Act" title="Dodd–Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act">Dodd–Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act</a>, signed into law by President Obama in July 2010, contained a supply chain sustainability provision in the form of the Conflict Minerals law. This law requires SEC-regulated companies to conduct third party audits of their supply chains in order to determine whether any tin, tantalum, tungsten, or gold (together referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Conflict_minerals" class="mw-redirect" title="Conflict minerals">conflict minerals</a></i>) is mined or sourced from the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, and create a report (available to the general public and SEC) detailing the due diligence efforts taken and the results of the audit.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The chain of suppliers and vendors to these reporting companies will be expected to provide appropriate supporting information.
</p><p>Incidents like the <a href="/wiki/2013_Savar_building_collapse" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Savar building collapse">2013 Savar building collapse</a>, with more than 1,100 victims, have led to widespread discussions about <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">corporate social responsibility</a> across global supply chains. Wieland and Handfield (2013) suggest that companies need to audit products and suppliers and that supplier auditing needs to go beyond direct relationships with first-tier suppliers. They also demonstrate that visibility needs to be improved if supply cannot be directly controlled and that smart and electronic technologies play a key role to improve visibility. Finally, they highlight that collaboration with local partners, across the industry and with universities is crucial to successfully managing social responsibility in supply chains.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Recent research proposes a two-phase approach for auditing multitier supply networks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Under this strategy, buyers first audit and drop noncompliant suppliers and then proceed to audit and rectify the remaining ones; when auditing an upper tier, the approach recommends selecting the "least valuable unaudited supplier" as the next candidate for auditing.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Circular_supply_chain_management">Circular supply chain management</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Circular supply chain management"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Circular Supply Chain Management (CSCM) is  "the configuration and coordination of the organizational functions marketing, sales, R&amp;D, production, logistics, IT, finance, and customer service within and across business units and organizations to close, slow, intensify, narrow, and dematerialise material and energy loops to minimize resource input into and waste and emission leakage out of the system, improve its operative effectiveness and efficiency and generate competitive advantages". By reducing resource input and waste leakage along the supply chain and configure it to enable the recirculation of resources at different stages of the product or service lifecycle, potential economic and environmental benefits can be achieved. These comprise e.g. a decrease in material and waste management cost and reduced emissions and <a href="/wiki/Resource_consumption" title="Resource consumption">resource consumption</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Supply_Chain_Engineering">Supply Chain Engineering</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Supply Chain Engineering"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Although it has the same goals as <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_engineering" title="Supply chain engineering">supply chain engineering</a>, supply chain management is focused on a more traditional <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">management</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">business</a> based approach, whereas supply chain engineering is focused on a <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_model" title="Mathematical model">mathematical model</a> based one.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ravi&#95;137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ravi-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Digitizing_supply_chains">Digitizing supply chains</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Digitizing supply chains"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Consultancies and media expect the performance efficacy of digitizing supply chains to be high.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/3D_printing" title="3D printing">Additive manufacturing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a> technology have emerged as the two technologies with some of the highest economic relevance.
</p>
<dl><dt>Additive manufacturing</dt>
<dd>The potential of additive manufacturing is particularly high in the production of spare parts, since its introduction can reduce warehousing costs of slowly rotating spare parts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Digitizing technology bears the potential to completely disrupt and restructure supply chains and enhance existing production routes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl>
<dl><dt>Blockchain</dt>
<dd>In comparison, research on the influence of blockchain technology on the supply chain is still in its early stages. The <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_writing" title="Conceptual writing">conceptual</a> literature has argued for a considerably long time that the highest performance efficacy is expected in the potential for automatic contract creation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Empirical_evidence" title="Empirical evidence">Empirical evidence</a> contradicts this hypothesis: the highest potential is expected in the arenas of verified <a href="/wiki/Customer_review" title="Customer review">customer reviews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Certification_mark" title="Certification mark">certifications</a> of product quality and standards.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, traditional supply chain has many drawbacks such as lack of transparency and trust, and some of them can be solved by blockchain technology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The technological features of blockchains support transparency and traceability of information, as well as high levels of reliability and immutability of records.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> That helps traditional supply chain management to be more efficient and reliable.</dd></dl>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Systems_and_value">Systems and value</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Systems and value"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Supply chain systems configure value for those that organize the networks. Value is the additional revenue over and above the costs of building the network. Co-creating value and sharing the benefits appropriately to encourage effective participation is a key challenge for any supply system. Tony Hines defines value as follows: "Ultimately it is the customer who pays the price for service delivered that confirms value and not the producer who simply adds cost until that point".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Hines2014&#95;20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hines2014-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Global_applications">Global applications</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Global applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Global supply chains pose challenges regarding both quantity and value. Supply and value chain trends include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">Globalization</a></li>
<li>Increased cross-border sourcing</li>
<li>Collaboration for parts of value chain with low-cost providers</li>
<li>Shared service centers for logistical and administrative functions</li>
<li>Increasingly global operations, which require increasingly global coordination and planning to achieve global optimums</li>
<li>Complex problems involve also midsized companies to an increasing degree</li></ul>
<p>These trends have many benefits for manufacturers because they make possible larger lot sizes, lower taxes, and better environments (e.g., culture, infrastructure, special tax zones, or sophisticated OEM) for their products. There are many additional challenges when the scope of supply chains is global. This is because with a supply chain of a larger scope, the lead time is much longer, and because there are more issues involved, such as multiple currencies, policies, and laws. The consequent problems include different currencies and valuations in different countries, different tax laws, different trading protocols, vulnerability to natural disasters and cyber threats,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and lack of transparency of cost and profit.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Roles_and_responsibilities">Roles and responsibilities</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Roles and responsibilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Supply chain professionals play major roles in the design and management of supply chains. In the design of supply chains, they help determine whether a product or service is provided by the firm itself (insourcing) or by another firm elsewhere (outsourcing). In the management of supply chains, supply chain professionals coordinate production among multiple providers, ensuring that production and transport of goods happen with minimal quality control or inventory problems. One goal of a well-designed and maintained supply chain for a product is to successfully build the product at minimal cost. Such a supply chain could be considered a competitive advantage for a firm.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Beyond design and maintenance of a supply chain itself, supply chain professionals participate in aspects of business that have a bearing on supply chains, such as <a href="/wiki/Sales_forecasting" class="mw-redirect" title="Sales forecasting">sales forecasting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quality_management" title="Quality management">quality management</a>, strategy development, <a href="/wiki/Customer_service" title="Customer service">customer service</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Systems_analysis" title="Systems analysis">systems analysis</a>. Production of a good may evolve over time, rendering an existing supply chain design obsolete. Supply chain professionals need to be aware of changes in production and business climate that affect supply chains and create alternative supply chains as the need arises.
</p><p>In a research project undertaken by <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">Michigan State University</a>'s Broad College of Business, with input from 50 participating organizations, the main issues of concern to supply chain managers were identified as capacity/resource availability, talent (<a href="/wiki/Recruitment" title="Recruitment">recruitment</a>), <a href="/wiki/Complexity" title="Complexity">complexity</a>, threats/challenges (<a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_risk_management" title="Supply chain risk management">supply chain risks</a>), compliance and cost/purchasing issues. Keeping up with frequent changes in regulation was identified as a particular concern.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Complexity within supply chains has also been highlighted in <i>Supply Chain Digest</i> and by <a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner</a> as a perennial challenge.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Supply chain consultants may provide expert knowledge in order to assess the productivity of a <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain" title="Supply chain">supply chain</a> and, ideally, to enhance its productivity. Supply chain consulting involves the transfer of knowledge on how to exploit existing assets through improved coordination and can hence be a source of competitive advantage: the role of the consultant is to help management by adding value to the whole process through the various sectors from the ordering of the raw materials to the final product.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In this regard, firms may either build internal teams of consultants to tackle the issue or engage external ones: companies choose between these two approaches taking into consideration various factors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The use of external consultants is a common practice among companies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The whole consulting process generally involves the analysis of the entire supply chain process, including the countermeasures or correctives to take to achieve a better overall performance.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Skills_and_competencies">Skills and competencies</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Skills and competencies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Supply chain professionals need to have knowledge of managing supply chain functions such as transportation, <a href="/wiki/Warehousing" class="mw-redirect" title="Warehousing">warehousing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_inventory_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Field inventory management">inventory management</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Production_planning" title="Production planning">production planning</a>. In the past, supply chain professionals emphasized <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistics</a> skills, such as knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Shipping" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping">shipping</a> routes, familiarity with warehousing equipment and <a href="/wiki/Distribution_center" title="Distribution center">distribution center</a> locations and footprints, and a solid grasp of <a href="/wiki/Freight_rate" title="Freight rate">freight rates</a> and fuel costs. More recently, supply chain management extends to logistical support across firms and management of global supply chains.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Supply chain professionals need to have an understanding of <a href="/wiki/Business_continuity" class="mw-redirect" title="Business continuity">business continuity</a> basics and strategies,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Tramarico <i>et al</i> noted that several processes from other disciplinary theories, including the resource-based view, supply chain design and interorganizational relationships are integral to a mature understanding of supply chain management.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A shortage of skilled supply chain professionals was highlighted in a study by the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> published in 2010, which highlighted plentiful supply of staff with "narrow technical skillsets" but shortages in the numbers of job applicants with "broader business skills".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Certification">Certification</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Certification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Individuals working in supply chain management can attain <a href="/wiki/Professional_certification" title="Professional certification">professional certification</a> by passing an exam developed by a third party certification organization. The purpose of certification is to guarantee a certain level of expertise in the field. The knowledge needed to pass a certification exam may be gained from several sources. Some knowledge may come from college courses, but most of it is acquired from a mix of on-the-job learning experiences, attending industry events, learning best practices with their peers, and reading books and articles in the field.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Certification organizations may provide certification workshops tailored to their exams.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="University_rankings">University rankings</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: University rankings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The following North American universities rank high in their master's education in the SCM World University 100 ranking, which was published in 2017 and which is based on the opinions of supply chain managers: <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">Michigan State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Penn State University">Penn State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tennessee" title="University of Tennessee">University of Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas at Austin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Michigan_University" title="Western Michigan University">Western Michigan University</a>. In the same ranking, the following European universities rank high: <a href="/wiki/Cranfield_School_of_Management" title="Cranfield School of Management">Cranfield School of Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlerick_Business_School" title="Vlerick Business School">Vlerick Business School</a>, <a href="/wiki/INSEAD" title="INSEAD">INSEAD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven_University_of_Technology" title="Eindhoven University of Technology">Eindhoven University of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Business_School" title="London Business School">London Business School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Business_School" title="Copenhagen Business School">Copenhagen Business School</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>The following universities rank high in the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Eduniversal" title="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</a> Best Masters ranking for supply chain and logistics: <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/KEDGE_Business_School" title="KEDGE Business School">KEDGE Business School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam_School_of_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotterdam School of Management">Rotterdam School of Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_del_Peru" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontificia Universidad Catolica del Peru">Pontificia Universidad Catolica del Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universidade_Nova_de_Lisboa" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidade Nova de Lisboa">Universidade Nova de Lisboa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna_University_of_Economics_and_Business" title="Vienna University of Economics and Business">Vienna University of Economics and Business</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Business_School" title="Copenhagen Business School">Copenhagen Business School</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Organizations">Organizations</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Organizations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A number of organizations provide certification in supply chain management, such as the Council of Supply Chain Management Professionals (CSCMP),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> IIPMR (International Institute for Procurement and Market Research), <a href="/wiki/APICS" class="mw-redirect" title="APICS">APICS</a> (the Association for Operations Management), ISCEA (<a href="/wiki/International_Supply_Chain_Education_Alliance" title="International Supply Chain Education Alliance">International Supply Chain Education Alliance</a>) and IoSCM (Institute of Supply Chain Management). APICS' certification is called <i>Certified Supply Chain Professional</i>, or CSCP, and ISCEA's certification is called the <i>Certified Supply Chain Manager</i> (CSCM), CISCM (Chartered Institute of Supply Chain Management) awards certificate as <i>Chartered Supply Chain Management Professional</i> (CSCMP). Another, the Institute for Supply Management, is developing one called the <i>Certified Professional in Supply Management</i> (CPSM)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Jacoby&#95;165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacoby-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> focused on the procurement and sourcing areas of supply chain management. The Supply Chain Management Association (SCMA) is the main certifying body for Canada with the designations having global reciprocity. The designation Supply Chain Management Professional (SCMP) is the title of the supply chain leadership designation.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Topics_addressed_by_selected_professional_supply_chain_certification_programmes">Topics addressed by selected professional supply chain certification programmes</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supply_chain_management&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Topics addressed by selected professional supply chain certification programmes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
